تعريف الدُّعاءِ وبيان أنَّ الدعاء ينفعُ الأحياء والأموات على دعائه عاجلاً أو آجلاً يُخرِجُه عن العَبثِيَّة. وجَزْمُنا الاعتقادَ بِنَفْعِ الدُّعاءِ كَمَا مِنَ القُرْآنِ وَعْدًا، أي: لأنَّ اللَّهَ وعَدَ في القُرآن حالَ كونِ ذلكَ الموعودِ به يُسْمَعُ مِن تلاوته، قال تعالى: ﴿وَقَالَ رَبُّكُمُ ادْعُونِي أَسْتَجِبْ لَكُمْ﴾ [غافر:60]، و﴿وَإِذَا سَأَلَكَ عِبَادِي عَنِي فَإِنِّي قَرِيبٌ أُجِيبُ دَعْوَةَ الدَّاعِ إِذَا دَعَانِ﴾ [البقرة:186]. وإطلاق هاتين الآيتين يُقيَّدُه قوله تعالى: ﴿فَيَكْشِفُ مَا تَدْعُونَ إِلَيْهِ إِن شَاءَ﴾ [الأنعام:41]، فالمَرادُ الإجابةُ المُصرَّحُ بها في حديث مناجاة موسى «وَإِنْ دعوني أستجب لهم، فإما أن يروه عاجلاً، وإِمَّا أَنْ أَصرِفَ سُوءًا، وإِمَّا أنْ أدَّخِره لهم في الآخرة». وفي كلام بعضهم: أنّ الإجابة تتنوع؛ فتارةً يقع المطلوب بعينه على الفور، وتارةً يقعُ ولكن يتأخَّر لحكمة فيه، وتارةً تَقَعُ الإجابةُ بغير عين المطلوب؛ حيثُ لا يكون في المطلوب مَصلحةٌ ناجزةٌ وفي الواقع مصلحة ناجزة، أو أصلح منها.
Definition of supplication and explaining that supplication benefits the living and the dead upon his supplication sooner or later - it removes it from futility. And our decisive belief in the benefit of supplication is a promise from the Qur'an, i.e., because Allah promised in the Qur'an, while that which is promised is heard from its recitation, He said: 'And your Lord said: Call upon Me, I will respond to you' [Ghafir:60], and 'When My servants ask you concerning Me, indeed I am near. I respond to the invocation of the supplicant when he calls upon Me' [Al-Baqarah:186]. But the absoluteness of these two verses is restricted by His saying: 'Then He removes that for which you call upon Him if He wills' [Al-An'am:41]. So what is intended is the response explicitly mentioned in the hadith of Musa's intimate conversation: 'If they call upon Me, I will respond to them, either they see it quickly, or I turn away evil, or I store it for them in the Hereafter.' And in the speech of some: that the response varies; sometimes the requested thing itself occurs immediately, sometimes it occurs but is delayed for a wisdom in it, and sometimes the response occurs with other than the requested thing itself; if there is no immediate benefit in the requested thing and there is an immediate benefit in what actually happens, or something more beneficial.
Source pages p. 466

Commentary
This passage defines supplication (du'a) and explains that it benefits both the living and the dead. It begins by stating that du'a, when offered sooner or later, removes futility. Then it asserts our decisive belief in its benefit based on the promise in the Qur'an. It quotes two verses: 'Call upon Me, I will respond to you' and 'I respond to the invocation of the supplicant when he calls upon Me.' It then notes that the absoluteness of these verses is restricted by another verse: 'Then He removes that for which you call upon Him if He wills.' The intended meaning is explained by the hadith of Moses' intimate conversation with Allah, where response can be immediate, by averting evil, or stored for the Hereafter. The passage further explains that responses vary: sometimes the exact request is granted immediately, sometimes with delay, and sometimes what is granted is different because the original request may not be in the person's best interest, but what is granted is more beneficial. Thus, the passage assures that du'a is never wasted.

Correction: The passage shows that response may be delayed or replaced with something better, so du'a is never futile.

Key Takeaway
Du'a always benefits because Allah responds in the most appropriate way, whether immediately, by averting harm, or by reserving reward for the Hereafter.

Why the Qur'an is the Specified Proof for Du'a
The author answers why the proof of du'a is from the Qur'an specifically.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the proof of du'a is specified to the Qur'an and that the indication is not limited to it.

Core Idea
The Qur'an is specified due to tawatur, not exclusive indication.

In this passage, Sanusi addresses a potential objection: why is the proof for du'a taken specifically from the Qur'an? He clarifies that it is due to the Qur'an's tawatur (mass transmission), not because the indication is limited to it. He then provides examples from the Prophet's own practice to show that du'a is also attested in other ways. This lesson unpacks that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the concise style of Sanusi.
2
Identify the main claim
The passage begins by stating that the specification of the Qur'an is due to tawatur, not because the indication is limited to it. This is the key point.
The author is responding to an implied objection.
3
Examine the evidence
The author then provides evidence from the Prophet's practice: he called upon his Lord in many situations. Note the three examples given.
These examples show that du'a is not confined to the Qur'an.
4
Understand the consensus
The passage ends by mentioning the agreement of the salaf and khalaf on this matter. This strengthens the proof.
Consensus is an important source of authority in Islam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتخصيص القرآنِ لِتواتُره، لا لِقَصْرِ الدَّلالة عليه، فقد دعا صلى الله عليه وسلم ربَّهُ في مواطن كثيرة كيوم بدر، وعلى قاتل أهل بئر معونة، وعلى المُستهزئين، وأجمع عليه السَّلفُ والخَلفُ.
And specifying the Qur'an is due to its tawatur (mass transmission), not because the indication is limited to it. For the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, called upon his Lord in many situations, like the day of Badr, and against the killer of the people of Bi'r Ma'unah, and against those who mocked him, and the predecessors and successors agreed upon it.
Source pages p. 467

Commentary
This passage addresses an anticipated objection: why is the proof for du'a taken specifically from the Qur'an? The answer is that the Qur'an is specified because it is mutawatir (mass-transmitted), not because the indication is limited to it. The author then provides evidence from the practice of the Prophet, peace be upon him, who called upon his Lord in many situations such as the day of Badr, against the killer of the people of Bi'r Ma'unah, and against those who mocked him. The salaf and khalaf (the early and later generations) have agreed upon this. Thus, the proof from the Qur'an is not exclusive; the Prophet's own practice also supports it.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Qur'an is the only source of proof for du'a.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the Qur'an is specified because of its tawatur, but the indication is not limited to it. The Prophet's own actions and the consensus of the community also serve as proof.

Key Takeaway
The Qur'an's specification as proof for du'a is due to its tawatur, not because other sources are invalid; the Prophet's practice and consensus also affirm du'a.

Etiquettes of Supplication
Enumerates recommended etiquettes of supplication.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the recommended etiquettes of supplication as enumerated by the author, including timings, preconditions, and structure.

Core Idea
Supplication has etiquettes that align the heart with Allah.

This lesson presents the etiquettes of du'a recommended by the author. These practices help the believer approach Allah with proper adab, maximizing the potential for acceptance. The passage lists specific times, actions, and words to include.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that it begins with 'ومن آداب الدعاء' and then lists items. Try to see the flow from times to actions to words.
The list is not exhaustive; it ends with 'والله أعلم'.
2
Identify each etiquette
Go through the list one by one. Make a mental note of each: seeking virtuous times (prostration, adhan), performing ablution and prayer, facing qiblah, raising hands, preceding with repentance, acknowledgment of sin and sincerity, opening with praise and blessings on the Prophet, asking by Allah's names, concluding with blessings, and also placing them in the middle.
3
Reflect on the wisdom
Consider why each etiquette is recommended. For example, seeking virtuous times shows awareness of divine mercy, and opening with praise shows humility. Think about how these etiquettes improve the quality of du'a.
This reflection helps internalize the adab.

Belief in Guardian and Recording Angels
Commentary explaining obligation of belief in guardian and recording angels

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that every accountable human being is assigned guardian angels who record all speech and actions, and that this belief is an obligatory part of the transmitted matters (sam'iyyat), covering both believers and disbelievers.

Core Idea
Every accountable human has guardian angels recording every deed.

This commentary on a verse from the Jawharat al-Tawhid explains the Islamic creed regarding the guardian angels (al-hafazah) and recording angels (al-katabah). The author emphasizes that this is a transmitted matter (sam'iyyah) that must be believed without rational proof. The passage clarifies that these angels are assigned to every adult human, whether believer or disbeliever, male or female, free or slave, and that they record everything, including permissible actions.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening verse and its translation
Begin by reading the poetic line that summarizes the belief in guardian angels. Notice the emphasis that they are 'chosen' and 'never neglect' anything.
2
Understand who is covered
The commentary specifies that 'every servant' means every accountable human (mukallaf), including disbelievers. This counters a possible misconception that only believers have guardian angels.
The text explicitly says 'mu'minan kana aw kafiran'.
3
Recognize the scope of recording
The angels record all speech and action, even the permissible (mubah). The commentary notes that recording does not automatically entail punishment or reward.
This is from the beginning of footnote (3), though the footnote is cut off.
4
Reflect on the theological implications
Believing in these angels reinforces accountability for every deed, as nothing is left unrecorded. This is a matter of faith (sam'iyyat) that must be accepted as revealed.
Connect to the learning objective.

Obligation of faith in the guardian angels and the recording angels of deeds among the angels. - 'Over every servant are guardians appointed and writers, chosen, they will not neglect, from his affair anything he does, even if he forgets, even the groaning in illness, as has been narrated.' Then he drew attention to a matter from the transmitted matters (al-sam`iyyat) whose belief is obligatory by his saying: 'Over every servant' (1) adult human, whether believer or disbeliever (2), male or female, free or slave, 'guardians' over what issues from him of speech or action. (3) (1) His saying: 'Over every servant' is attached to 'appointed', i.e., guardians appointed over every servant, and it includes humans, jinn, and angels. As for humans and jinn, it is obvious. As for angels, it is said there is hesitation, and the apparent view is that there are no guardians over them. Al-Shanwani. Al-Laqani said in his small commentary: Al-Jazuli hesitated over jinn and angels, whether they have guardians or not... then he affirmed that jinn have guardians, and he considered the statement unlikely for angels, and I have not found it for jinn from others. These discussions have transmitted foundations. See: Hidayat al-Murid vol. 2, pp. 936-937. (2) His saying: 'or disbeliever' and it does not necessitate requital in paradise from the recording. Al-Amir. And because it preserves his breaths and his deeds upon him and for him. And al-Nawawi deemed correct that if a disbeliever does beautiful actions that do not require intention, like charity and maintaining family ties, then embraces Islam, he is rewarded for them, because their reward is written for him. And the expression of al-Khatib al-Shirbini in his commentary on His saying 'Noble recording [angels]' (al-Infitar 11) is: They differed over disbelievers: are there guardians over them? It is said: No, because their affair is apparent and their action is one. He said: 'The criminals will be known by their mark' (al-Rahman 41). And it is said: They have guardians, and this is apparent from His saying 'Nay! But you deny the Judgment. And indeed, [appointed] over you are guardians, noble recording [angels]' (al-Infitar 9-11), and His saying 'And as for he who is given his record behind his back' (al-Inshiqaq 10). So He informed that they have a book and that they have guardians. If it is said: What does the one on his right write when he has no good deed? The answer is: The one on his right is with the permission of his companion a witness over that even if he does not write. So in this verse is evidence that the witness does not testify except after knowledge, because of their description as being 'guardians, noble, recording, knowing what you do'. That indicates that they are knowers of them until they write them. So when they write them, they are at the time of performing testimony. End of the expression of al-Khatib, by way of al-Shanwani. (3) His saying: 'of speech or action' includes the permissible, because writing does not entail punishment or reward, and he relied on=
Source pages p. 469

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a line of poetry from the Jawharat al-Tawhid, explaining the obligation of believing in the guardian angels (al-hafazah) and recording angels (al-katabah). It begins by stating the obligation to believe in these angels. Then it quotes the verse: 'Over every servant are guardians appointed and writers, chosen, they will not neglect, from his affair anything he does, even if he forgets...' The commentator draws attention to this matter from the transmitted matters (al-sam`iyyat) that must be believed. He then explains the phrase 'over every servant' (bi-kulli `abd), specifying that it refers to every accountable human being (mukallaf) whether believer or disbeliever, male or female, free or slave. Then he explains 'guardians' (hafizun) as those who guard what issues from the servant in terms of speech or action. The footnotes provide additional scholarly discussion: Footnote (1) discusses the scope of 'every servant' — it includes humans, jinn, and angels, but there is hesitation about angels having guardians. Al-Shanwani states the apparent view is that angels do not have guardians. Al-Laqani mentions that al-Jazuli hesitated but concluded that jinn have guardians and angels do not. Footnote (2) addresses the case of disbelievers: they have guardian angels even though they will not be rewarded in paradise, because the angels preserve their actions and breaths. Al-Nawawi is cited for the ruling that if a disbeliever does good deeds without needing intention (like charity) and later embraces Islam, he is rewarded. Al-Khatib al-Shirbini's interpretation of relevant Quranic verses is quoted to show that disbelievers have guardians and that the angels record their deeds and witness them. Footnote (3) begins to explain that 'speech or action' includes permissible actions, because writing does not necessarily entail reward or punishment. This footnote is cut off at the end of the page. The passage thus provides a detailed theological clarification of the belief in guardian angels.

Misconception: Only believers have guardian angels.
Correction: The text explicitly states that every accountable human, whether believer or disbeliever, has guardian angels.

D) Only angels

Key Takeaway
Every accountable human being, believer or disbeliever, has appointed guardian angels who record all speech and actions, and this belief is an obligatory part of Islamic faith derived from transmitted sources.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
You have guardian angels assigned to you at this very moment. Are you living as if that is true? When you are alone, do you still act as if you are being watched? What is one thing you will do today to increase your awareness of their presence?

Belief in Guardian and Recording Angels
Author explains duty to believe in guardian and recording angels, their scope, and a hadith reconciliation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic belief in the guardian and recording angels, including their scope, the types of actions they record, and how to reconcile the hadith about angels not entering houses with certain objects.

Core Idea
Guardian angels record every action, intention, and approval—even forgotten ones—and never leave except during three bodily needs.

This lesson establishes the duty to believe in the guardian and recording angels. The author explains that these angels are assigned to every accountable human and record every single thing, including intentions and tacit approvals. He also addresses an apparent conflict with a hadith about angels not entering certain houses, showing that the hadith refers to mercy angels, not guardian angels.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Pay attention to the verse line and the prose explanation that follows. This will give you an overview of the lesson's content.
2
Identify the scope of the angels
Notice that the author specifies 'every servant' includes all accountable humans—believer or disbeliever, male or female, free or slave. Understand that the angels guard and record all actions.
The angels are assigned by Allah and never leave the person.
3
Categories of recorded actions
The passage lists three categories: speech, action, and belief. Also three inner states: intention, determination, and tacit approval. Mark these in the text.
Even forgotten actions and groans in illness are recorded.
4
Exception to the angels' constant presence
The author states that guardian angels only leave during three specific bodily needs: defecation, janabah (post-sexual impurity), and ghusl (ritual bath). This is based on a hadith of Ibn Abbas.
This exception shows that guardian angels are always present except for these natural functions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

For every servant there are guardians, assigned, and writers, chosen, they will not neglect anything of his command, (whether) done or even forgotten, until the groan in illness, as transmitted. Then he drew attention to a matter from the transmitted things (al-sam'iyyat) that must be believed, by his saying: (For every servant) accountable from humans, whether believer or disbeliever, male or female, free or slave, (guardians) for what issues from him of speech, or action, or belief, (whether) intention, or determination, or tacit approval, (assigned), meaning: Allah Almighty assigned them to the servant, they do not leave him even if he is in a house containing a bell, or dog, or image. As for the hadith: 'Angels do not enter a house containing a bell' and the like, what is meant is the angels of mercy, not the guardian angels; for they do not leave him due to any of that except in one of three needs: defecation, janabah, and ghusl, as came in the hadith of Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them both.

Commentary
This passage states the necessity of believing in the guardian and recording angels (al-hafazah wa al-katabah) as a matter of sam'iyyat (transmitted beliefs). The author first quotes the poem line establishing that every servant has guardians and writers who never neglect anything. Then he explains that this applies to every accountable human being (mukallaf min al-bashar), regardless of faith, gender, or status. These angels guard and record everything that issues from the person: speech, action, belief, including intention (hamm), determination (azm), and tacit approval (taqrir). The angels are assigned by Allah and never leave the person, even if the person is in a house with a bell, dog, or image—things that would repel the angels of mercy. The author then addresses a potential objection: the hadith stating angels do not enter a house with a bell. He resolves it by distinguishing between the guardian angels (al-hafazah) and the angels of mercy (mala'ikat al-rahma). The guardian angels are not affected by these impediments. However, they do leave during three specific bodily functions: defecation, janabah (post-sexual impurity), and ghusl (ritual bath), as confirmed by a hadith of Ibn Abbas. This preserves the doctrine while harmonizing with the apparent conflict.

The Obligation to Believe in Guardian and Recording Angels
States obligation and identifies guardian angels as recording scribes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the obligation to believe in guardian and recording angels and how the Qur'an links them as the same angels chosen by Allah.

Core Idea
Guardian angels are the same as recording angels, both obligatory to believe in.

This lesson establishes that belief in guardian angels (al-ḥafaẓah) and recording angels (al-kātibūn) is obligatory. The author explains that the Qur'anic term 'guardians' is connected with 'scribes chosen' to show that these angels are specially selected for both roles.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once to get the rhythm. Then read the translation to grasp the meaning.
Notice the verse reference is implicit; the author quotes the phrase 'wa-kātibūn khīrah'.
2
Understand the link between guardians and scribes
The author says that 'guardians' (ḥāfiẓūn) is coupled with 'scribes chosen' for explanation (tafsīr). This means the same angels guard and record deeds.
The word 'khīrah' means chosen, highlighting Allah's selection.
3

Ponder why belief in these angels is obligatory. They are constantly with you, recording your deeds.

Commentary
This passage defines the obligation of belief in two categories of angels: the guardian angels (al-ḥafaẓah) who protect the person, and the recording angels (al-kātibūn) who record deeds. This is supported by a hadith from Ibn ʿAbbās. Finally, a minority opinion is noted that permissible (mubāḥ) acts are not recorded by the angels.

Clarifies hadith and lists exceptions for guardian angels

Core Idea

A common hadith says angels do not enter houses with bells or dogs. This lesson clarifies that this refers specifically to angels of mercy, not the guardian/recording angels. The guardian angels remain with a person except during three unavoidable states: defecation, sexual impurity, and ritual washing.

Are the Mu'aqqibat Distinct from the Recording Angels?
Author argues for distinction between mu'aqqibat and katabah via al-Qurṭubī.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the arguments that distinguish the guardian angels (mu'aqqibat) from the recording angels (katabah) based on Qur'anic evidence and transmitted reports.

Core Idea
Guardian angels never leave, so they can't be the ones asked about leaving.

The Qur'an mentions both successive angels who guard (mu'aqqibat) and recording angels (katabah). Some scholars have argued they are the same group, but al-Qurṭubī presents three compelling reasons why they are distinct. This passage examines his reasoning and its scriptural basis.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation.
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the main claim and the supporting arguments.
The passage contains a view from al-Ṣaghīr and detailed reasoning from al-Qurṭubī.
2
Identify the main claim.
The passage argues that the mu'aqqibat are not the same as the katabah. The conjunction in the verse indicates distinct groups.
3
Examine al-Qurṭubī's three arguments.
Look for the three points: no report of guardians leaving, no distinction between night/day guardians, and the implication of the verse 'How did you leave My servants?'.
Each argument reinforces the distinction.
4
Understand the verse implication.
The questioning about 'leaving' only makes sense if the angels sometimes depart, which the guardians never do.
This is the strongest evidence.
5
Reflect on the broader significance.
Consider how this distinction affects our understanding of angelic roles and the divine command.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والذي في الصغير أن العطف للتغاير (٤) لما ذكره بعضهم من أن في قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَهُ مُعَقِّبَاتٌ مِنْ بَيْنِ يَدَيْهِ وَمِنْ خَلْفِهِ يَحْفَظُونَهُ مِنْ أَمْرِ اللَّهِ﴾ غير الكاتبين. قال القرطبي: ويقويه أنه لم ينقل أن الحفظة يفارقون العبد، ولا أن حفظة الليل غير حفظة النهار، وأنه لو كانوا هم الحفظة لم يقع الاكتفاء في السؤال منهم عن حالة الترك دون غيرها في قوله تعالى: «كيف تركتم عبادي؟».
And what is in 'al-Ṣaghīr' is that the conjunction is for differentiation (4), due to what some mentioned that in His statement, exalted: 'For him are successive [angels] before him and behind him, guarding him by the command of Allah' (Qur'an 13:11) are other than the scribes. Al-Qurṭubī said: And it strengthens this that it has not been transmitted that the guardians leave the servant, nor that the guardians of the night are other than the guardians of the day, and that if they were the guardians, the questioning of them about the state of abandonment alone without other things would not have sufficed in His statement, exalted: 'How did you leave My servants?'
Source pages p. 472

Commentary
This passage examines the relationship between the angels referred to as 'mu'aqqibat' (successive angels) in verse 13:11 of the Qur'an and the recording angels (al-kātibūn). One view, mentioned in a smaller commentary (al-Ṣaghīr), is that the conjunction of 'guardians' and 'scribes' indicates they are distinct groups (taghāyur). Al-Qurṭubī supports this view with three arguments: (1) There is no transmitted report that the guardian angels ever leave a person, even during the three exceptions mentioned earlier. (2) It is not reported that the angels of the night are different from those of the day, implying they are the same continuous guardians. (3) In the Qur'anic verse where Allah asks the angels 'How did you leave My servants?' (6:94, 7:8), the question is asked of angels who are assumed to have left the servants temporarily; but if the guardian angels never leave, they would not be addressed in this manner. Thus, the angels being questioned are likely a separate group (e.g., the recording angels who may delegate temporarily).

Key Terms
المعقبات
الكاتبون
الحفظة
التغاير
القرطبي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The mu'aqqibat and katabah are the same angels with different functions.
Correction: Al-Qurṭubī argues they are distinct because the guardians never leave, while the katabah (or other angels) are questioned about leaving.

Checkpoint

B) The guardian angels never leave the servant, so they cannot be the ones questioned in 'How did you leave My servants?'
C) The recording angels are not mentioned in the Qur'an.

Key Takeaway
The mu'aqqibat (guardians) are distinct from the recording angels because they never leave the person, as argued by al-Qurṭubī.

The Recording Angels: Identity, Number, and Writing
Discussion on the identity and number of angels who record deeds.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the obligation to believe in the guardian and recording angels, the scholarly debate on whether they are the same group, their number as per hadith, and the reality of their writing.

Core Idea
Angels record every deed with real instruments, and their exact number and identity are matters of careful interpretation.

This lesson brings together several interconnected points about the angels who guard and record human deeds. We begin with the general obligation, then examine a key grammatical debate about whether guards and scribes are identical, followed by a hadith specifying their precise number and positions, and finally an affirmation that their writing is literal and physical.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening obligation and the grammatical debate
Start by reading the first part of the passage which states the obligation and introduces the two interpretations of the conjunction 'wa' in 'hafizoon wa katiboon'.
Pay attention to the terms 'tafsir' and 'taghayur'.
2
Understand the two interpretations and al-Qurtubi's evidence
After reading, identify the two views: that the 'wa' means explanation (same angels) or difference (distinct groups). Note how al-Qurtubi argues for the latter.
3
Study the hadith on the number and positions of angels
Read the hadith from at-Tabarani. List the ten angels mentioned for day and night and their positions.
The hadith supports both interpretations depending on how the conjunction is understood.
4
Reflect on the reality of the writing
Finally, note the statement that the writing is 'haqiqi' with instruments like paper and ink. This upholds the apparent meaning of the texts.
This counters any metaphorical interpretation.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجوب الإيمان بالحفظة وكتبة الأعمال من الملائكة وعطف على «حافظون» للتفسير قوله: (وكاتبون خيرة) أي: اختارهم الله لذلك، هذا ما صرح به المصنف رحمه الله تعالى في شرحه الكبير أن المعقبات والذي في الصغير أن العطف للتغاير؛ لما ذكره بعضهم من في قوله تعالى: {وله معقبات من بين يديه ومن خلفه يحفظونه من أمر الله} [الرعد: 11] غير الكاتبين. قال القرطبي: ويقويه أن لم ينقل أن الحفظة يفارقون العبد، ولا أن حفظة الليل غير حفظة النهار، وأنه لو كانوا هم الحفظة لم يقع الاكتفاء في السؤال منهم عن حالة الترك دون غيرها في قوله تعالى: «كيف تركتم عبادي؟» وعند الطبراني: أن عثمان سأل النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم عن عدد الملائكة الموكلين بالآدمي، فقال: «لكل آدمي عشرة بالليل وعشرة بالنهار، واحد عن يمينه، وآخر عن شماله، واثنان بين يديه ومن خلفه، واثنان على حاجبيه، وآخر قابض على ناصيته، فإن تواضع رفعه، وإن تكبر وضعه، واثنان على شفتيه ليس يحفظان عليه إلا الصلاة على محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم، والعاشر يحرسه من الحية أن تدخل فاه»، ويؤخذ من الحديث أن كل عبد وكل به جمع من الحفظة، هذا على جعل العطف للتفسير، وأما على جعله للمغايرة فهو لمطابقة قوله: بكل عبد؛ لأن كل واحد من العباد إنما عليه ملكان؛ وهما: الرقيب والعتيد، من ملائكة الليل والنهار. والكتب حقيقي؛ بآلة وقرطاس ومداد يعلمها الله سبحانه، حملا للنصوص على ظواهرها؛ ففي حديث معاذ بن جبل أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم
The obligation to believe in the guardian angels and the scribes of deeds from among the angels. And the conjunction (waw) on 'hafizoon' is for explanation (tafsir) of His saying: 'and scribes, chosen' meaning: Allah chose them for that. This is what the author (may Allah have mercy on him) explicitly stated in his large commentary: that the 'mu'aqqibat' and [the view] in the small [commentary] is that the conjunction is for difference (taghayur); because some have mentioned that in His saying: 'For him are successive [angels] before him and behind him, guarding him by the command of Allah' [Ar-Ra'd: 11] are other than the scribes. Al-Qurtubi said: And it is strengthened by the fact that it has not been transmitted that the guardian angels leave the servant, nor that the night guardians are different from the day guardians, and that if they were the guardians, the question 'How did you leave My servants?' would not suffice without [asking about] other states. And from at-Tabarani: that Uthman asked the Prophet (peace be upon him) about the number of angels entrusted with the human being, and he said: 'For every human being there are ten by night and ten by day: one on his right, another on his left, two before him and two behind him, two on his eyebrows, another grasping his forelock — if he is humble, he raises him, and if he is arrogant, he lowers him — and two on his lips who record for him nothing but the prayer upon Muhammad (peace be upon him), and the tenth guards him from the snake entering his mouth.' And it is taken from the hadith that every servant has a group of guardian angels entrusted with him — this according to making the conjunction for explanation. As for making it for difference, it is to match His saying: 'with every servant'; because every single servant has only two angels over him: the Raqib and the 'Atid, from the angels of night and day. And the writing is real (haqiqi), with an instrument and paper and ink known to Allah Exalted, carrying the texts on their apparent meanings; for in the hadith of Mu'adh ibn Jabal that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) ...
Source pages p. 472

Commentary
This passage is a theological discussion on the obligation to believe in the angels who guard and record deeds. It begins by stating the general obligation. Then it examines the conjunction (waw) in the phrase 'hafizoon (guardians) and katiboon (scribes)' from the Quran. The author clarifies that there are two interpretations: either the waw is for tafsir (explanation), meaning the guardians are the same as the scribes, or it is for taghayur (difference), meaning they are distinct groups. The author mentions that in his larger commentary he held the tafsir view, while in the smaller commentary he held the taghayur view, the latter supported by some exegetes who see the 'mu'aqqibat' (successive angels) in verse 11 of Surat ar-Ra'd as separate from the scribes. Al-Qurtubi is then quoted to strengthen the taghayur view: it is not reported that the guardians ever leave the servant, nor that night and day guardians are different, and the Quranic question to them about 'how did you leave My servants?' would be insufficient if they were the same as the scribes, since scribes record everything. The passage then presents a hadith from at-Tabarani in which Uthman asks the Prophet about the number of angels with each person. The Prophet enumerates ten by night and ten by day, describing their positions and functions, including two on the lips who only record blessings on the Prophet, and one who guards against snakes. The hadith supports the view that many angels (a collection) are entrusted with each person. The author notes that this fits the tafsir interpretation (guardians are many). If the conjunction is for taghayur, then the hadith is understood differently: the many angels are guardians, but the scribes are only two (Raqib and 'Atid) per person, matching the phrase 'with every servant' from another verse. Finally, the passage asserts that the act of writing is real (haqiqi), involving instruments like paper and ink known to Allah, upholding the literal apparent meaning of the texts, as indicated by a hadith from Mu'adh ibn Jabal.

Key Terms
حفظة (hafazah)
كتبة (katabah)
معقبات (mu'aqqibat)
رقيب (Raqib)
عتيد ('Atid)
تفسير (tafsir)
تغاير (taghayur)
قرطاس (qirtas)
مداد (midad)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the guardian angels and recording angels are always the same.
Correction: The passage shows a scholarly difference: some interpret the conjunction as explanation (same), others as differentiation (distinct). The hadith can accommodate both views.

Checkpoint

B) Whether the 'waw' conjunction indicates explanation (tafsir) or difference (taghayur)
C) Whether the angels write with ink or with light
D) Whether the number of angels is ten or twenty per person

Key Takeaway
The belief in recording angels includes accepting their multiplicity, specific assignments per person, and the literal nature of their record-keeping with real instruments.

?
The hadith mentions that two angels on your lips only record the prayer upon the Prophet. What does this tell you about the value of that prayer? Are you sincere in sending it often?
?
Consider the angels on your right and left: are you more concerned with what people see than what the angels record? How can you realign your priorities starting now?

The Ten Angels by Night and Day: Their Positions and Duties
Hadith describing ten angels by night and ten by day with positions and duties, plus reconciliation with two angels.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific roles of the ten angels assigned to each human being as described in the hadith, and how this relates to the two recording angels (Raqīb and 'Atīd).

Core Idea
Every person is surrounded by ten angels by day and ten by night, each with a specific duty.

This hadith reveals the extensive angelic supervision over every human being. While we often focus on the two recording angels, this narration expands the picture to a whole team of guardians and recorders. As we read, pay attention to the positions and duties mentioned, and then see how the commentator reconciles this with the well-known two angels.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith slowly
Read the Arabic passage carefully, noting the positions mentioned: right, left, front, back, eyebrows, forelock, lips, and the tenth guardian.
The hadith is attributed to Uthman ibn Affan (رضي الله عنه).
2
Reflect on the duties
Consider what each angel does: recording good and bad, guarding, humbling or raising based on humility/arrogance, recording only salawat, and protection from snakes entering the mouth.
3
Study the commentary's reconciliation
Read the commentator's explanation about the conjunction being explanatory vs. differentiating, and how it relates to the two angels (Raqīb and 'Atīd) mentioned in Surah Qaf.
This clarifies the relationship between the ten angels and the two recording angels.
4
Ponder the significance
Ask yourself: Why does this multiplicity matter? It shows the comprehensive care and accountability God has established for each person, reflecting His justice and mercy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم السمعيات بالآدمي، فقال: «لكلِّ آدمي عشرة بالليل وعشرة بالنَّهار، واحد عن يمينه، وآخرُ عن شماله، واثنان بين يديه ومن خلفه، واثنان على حاجبيه، وآخر قابض على نَاصيته، فإن تواضع رفعه، وإنْ تكبّر وضعه، واثنان على شفتيه ليس يحفظان عليه إلّا الصَّلاة على محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم، والعاشر يحرسه مِن الحيَّة أنْ تدخل فاه» ويؤخذ من الحديث أنَّ كلَّ عبدٍ وُكِّلَ به جمعٌ مِن الحَفَظَةِ، هذا على جعل العطف للتفسير، وأمَّا على جعله للمُغايرة فهو لمطابقة قوله: بكل عبد ; لأنَّ كل واحد من العباد إنما عليه ملكان ; وهما: الرَّقِيبُ والعَتِيدُ، مِن ملائكة الليل والنهار.
Section on sam‘iyyāt. Concerning the human being, he said: 'Every human has ten [angels] by night and ten by day: one on his right, another on his left, two in front of him and behind him, two on his eyebrows, another grasping his forelock—if he humbles himself, He raises him, and if he becomes arrogant, He abases him—and two on his lips that only record for him prayers upon Muhammad (peace be upon him), and the tenth guards him from the snake entering his mouth.' It is derived from the hadith that every servant is entrusted with a group of guardians—this if the conjunction is explanatory; but if it is for differentiation, then it corresponds to his statement 'with every servant'—because every single servant only has two angels over him: they are al-raqīb (the Watcher) and al-‘atīd (the Present), from the angels of night and day.
Source pages p. 473

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal proof from hadith regarding the number and roles of the recording angels (al-ḥafaẓah). It begins by stating that every human has ten angels by night and ten by day, each with a specific position and duty: one on the right records good deeds, one on the left records bad deeds, two in front and two behind guard him as per Surah Ra‘d 13:11, two on his eyebrows, one on his forelock that humbles or abases, two on his lips recording only blessings on the Prophet, and the tenth protects him from snakes entering his mouth—symbolizing protection from harmful speech or evil whispers. The commentary then notes that this hadith indicates each servant has a group of guardians, but when the conjunction is taken as differentiating, it matches another hadith that each servant has only two angels: the Raqīb and ‘Atīd (from Surah Qaf 50:18), who are from the angels of night and day. The point is to reconcile the apparent multiplicity with the two main recording angels; the ten are separate or a fuller description of the guardians.

The Reality of the Recording of Deeds
Claim that recording is literal, supported by hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the recording of deeds by angels is a literal reality involving physical instruments, as affirmed by the hadith of Mu'adh.

Core Idea
The recording of deeds is real—with pen, ink, and paper known to Allah.

Sanusi begins by affirming the reality of the recording of deeds. He insists that this recording is literal, not metaphorical, and is done using actual instruments. To support this, he invokes the hadith of Mu'adh ibn Jabal, which describes the tongue as a pen and saliva as ink. This passage establishes the foundational principle that texts should be taken at their apparent meaning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the reality of recording
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Sanusi asserts the recording is real (ḥaqīqī).
The phrase 'ḥamlan li-l-nuṣūṣ ʿalā ẓawāhirihā' is key.
2
Identify the supporting evidence
Identify the hadith of Mu'adh that is cited as proof. Focus on how it shows a concrete physical process.
The tongue becomes the pen, saliva the ink.
3
Reflect on the literal interpretation
Ask yourself: Why is it important that this recording be real and not metaphorical? Consider the implications for accountability.
This connects to the broader theme of divine justice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والكتب حقيقي; بآلةٍ وقرطاس ومِدَادٍ يعلمها الله سبحانه، حملا للنصوص على ظواهرها ; ففي حديث معاذ بن جبل قال: إن الله لطفَ الملكين الحافظين حتى أجلَسَهُما على النَّاجذين، وجعل لسانه قلمَهُما، وريقه مِدَادَهما» وخرَّجه الدَّيْلمي من حديث عليّ بلفظ: لِسَانُ الإنسانِ قَلَمُ المَلَك، وَرِيقُه مِدَادُه والمراد بـ«النَّاجذين»: آخِرُ الأضْرَاس الأيمن والأيسر، وقيل: محلهما من الإنسان عاتقاه، وقيل: ذقنه، وقيل: شفتاه، وقيل: عنفقته (٤)، وفي حديث معاذ من الأبلغية ما ليس في غيره (ه) ومَلَكُ الحَسنات من ناحية اليمين أمين أو أمير على كاتب السيئات من ناحية اليسار فإن مشى كان أحدهما أمامه والآخر وراءه، وإن قعد كان
And the recording is real—with an instrument, paper, and ink that God knows, by carrying the texts upon their apparent meanings. For in the hadith of Mu‘ādh ibn Jabal, he said: 'Indeed God refined the two guardian angels until He seated them upon the molars (al-nājidhayn), and made his tongue their pen and his saliva their ink.' And al-Daylamī narrated it from the hadith of ‘Alī with the wording: 'The tongue of a human is the pen of the angel, and his saliva is its ink.' And what is meant by 'al-nājidhayn' is the last right and left molars; and it is said: their place from the human is his collarbones; and it is said: his chin; and it is said: his lips; and it is said: his mentum (the hair under the lower lip). And in the hadith of Mu‘ādh there is a rhetorical potency not found in others. And the angel of good deeds from the direction of the right is a trustee or commander over the writer of evil deeds from the direction of the left. So if he walks, one of them is in front of him and the other behind him; and if he sits, [he?/they?] was/were...
Source pages p. 473

Commentary
This passage asserts that the recording of deeds (al-kitāb) is real (ḥaqīqī), meaning it actually occurs using physical instruments—a tool, paper, and ink—known only to God. This is based on taking scriptural texts at their apparent meaning (ẓawāhir). To support this, it cites the hadith of Mu‘ādh ibn Jabal (may God be pleased with him) in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) said that God refined the two guardian angels, seating them on the molars (al-nājidhayn), and made the human’s tongue their pen and his saliva their ink. This hadith is also narrated by al-Daylamī from ‘Alī (may God be pleased with him) with similar wording. The passage then explains what is meant by 'al-nājidhayn': the last molars on the right and left. Several alternative interpretations are given: the collarbones, the chin, the lips, or the tuft of hair under the lower lip. The commentator notes that the hadith of Mu‘ādh is particularly eloquent in its warning about the tongue, as it emphasizes that the tongue itself becomes the instrument of recording. The passage concludes with additional details about the arrangement of the angels: the angel of good deeds on the right is a trustee (amīn) or commander (amīr) over the angel of evil deeds on the left, and their positions change depending on whether the person is walking or sitting (though the final part is cut off).

قلم

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the recording of deeds is metaphorical or purely spiritual, without any physical instruments.
Correction: This passage affirms the recording is literal ('ḥaqīqī') with real instruments (pen, paper, ink), as supported by the apparent meaning of the hadith.

Key Takeaway

The Hadith of the Two Angels on the Molars
Explanatory details of the hadith and angel arrangement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the detailed description of the two guardian angels in the hadith, including their seating on the molars, the various interpretations of 'al-nājidhayn', and the arrangement of the angels of good and evil deeds.

Core Idea
Your tongue is the angel’s pen; your saliva is its ink.

The hadith of Mu‘ādh provides a vivid picture of how the angels record deeds. This passage explores the precise meaning of 'al-nājidhayn' (the molars) and the special role of the angel of good deeds as a trustee over the angel of evil deeds. Understanding these details reinforces the seriousness of every word we speak.

The Obligation of Belief in the Guardian Angels and Their Seating on the Molars
Author states the obligation and describes the two guardian angels seated on the molars.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic doctrine regarding the two guardian angels assigned to every human, their unique seating on the molars, and the metaphorical description of their recording using the tongue as pen.

Core Idea
The angels record your deeds using your own tongue as pen and saliva as ink.

The author begins by affirming the obligation of believing in the recording angels (al-ḥafaẓah) and elaborates on a striking description from the Prophet (peace be upon him) about two angels seated on the molars. This vivid metaphor emphasizes the immediacy and thoroughness of divine record-keeping.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the two guardian angels
Read the Arabic passage that starts with the obligation and describes the angels seated on the molars. Pay attention to the word 'al-nājidhayn' and its interpretations.
2
Understand the metaphor of pen and ink
Note that the tongue is the pen and saliva the ink, meaning the angels record every word spoken. This highlights the importance of speech.
The hadith of Mu'adh emphasizes the tongue's role in sin.
3
Reflect on the obligation of belief
This passage is not just descriptive; it establishes a doctrinal obligation. Consider why belief in these angels is necessary for a Muslim.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجوب الإيمان بالحفظة وكتبة الأعمال من الملائكة
قال: إن الله لطفَ الملكين الحافظين حتى أجلَسَهُما على النَّاجذين، وجعل لسانه قلمَهُما، وريقه مِدادَهما» وخرَّجه الدَّيْلمي من حديث عليّ بلفظ : لِسَانُ الإنسانِ قَلَمُ المَلَك، وَرِيقُه مِدَادُه» والمراد بـ«النَّاجذين»: آخِرُ الأضْرَاس الأيمن والأيسر ، وقيل : محلهما من الإنسان عاتقاه ، وقيل : ذقنه ، وقيل : شفتاه ، وقيل : عنفقته، وفي حديث معاذ من الأبلغية ما ليس في غيره
ومَلَكُ الحَسنات من ناحية اليمين أمين أو أمير على كاتب السيئات من ناحية اليسار فإن مشى كان أحدهما أمامه والآخر وراءه، وإن قعد كان أحدهما على يمينه والآخر على يساره، وإنْ رَقَدَ كان أحدهما عند رأسه والآخر عند رجليه كما رُوي عن مجاهد: «لا يتغيَّران ما دامَ حيًّا»، وقيل: بل لكل يوم وليلة مَلَكان يتعاقبان عند صلاة العصر وصلاة الصبح، ويؤرخون ما يكتبون من أعمال العباد بالأيَّام والجُمَع والأعوام والأماكن. (لَنْ يُهْمِلُوا)، أي: لا يَتْرُكونَ مِنْ أَمْرِهِ شَيْئًا فَعَلْ) المرادُ مِن الفعل ما يعمُّ القولَ وغيره، كما ذكره أولاً ؛ إذ الكتابة ليست مُختصَّةً بالأقوال، بل تكون في الأفعال، والاعتقادات، والنيَّات، كذكر القلب سرًّا بعلامة يعرفونه بها، ففي حديث حجاج بن دينار: قلت لأبي مِعْشَر : الرَّجل يذكر الله في نفسه ، كيف تكتبه الملائكة ؟ قال : يجدون الرّيح»، وفي حديث ابن عمر قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: إذا كذب العبد كذبة تباعد عنه الملك ميلًا مِن نَتن ما جاء به.
The obligation of belief in the guardian angels and the recorders of deeds from among the angels. He said: Verily, Allah refined the two guardian angels until He seated them on the molars, and made their tongue their pen, and their saliva their ink. And al-Daylami extracted it from the hadith of Ali with the wording: 'The tongue of the human is the pen of the angel, and his saliva is his ink.' And what is meant by 'al-nājidhayn' is the last right and left molars. And it is said: their place on the human is his shoulders, and it is said: his chin, and it is said: his lips, and it is said: his mustache. And in the hadith of Mu'adh there is a greater emphasis than in others. And the angel of good deeds on the right side is a trustee or an overseer over the recorder of evil deeds on the left side. If he walks, one of them is in front of him and the other behind him; if he sits, one is on his right and the other on his left; if he lies down, one is by his head and the other by his feet, as transmitted from Mujahid: 'They do not change as long as he lives.' And it is said: rather for every day and night there are two angels who alternate at the afternoon prayer and the morning prayer, and they date what they write of the deeds of the servants with days, weeks, years, and places. (They will not neglect), meaning: they do not leave out anything of his matter that he has done. What is meant by 'act' includes speech and other things, as he mentioned first; for writing is not specific to words, but rather it includes actions, beliefs, and intentions, like the heart's remembrance secretly with a sign by which they recognize it. In the hadith of Hajjaj ibn Dinar: I said to Abu Ma'shar: A man remembers Allah in himself, how do the angels write it? He said: They perceive the scent. And in the hadith of Ibn Umar: The Messenger of Allah said: 'When a servant tells a lie, the angel moves away from him a mile due to the stench of what he has brought.'
Source pages p. 474

Commentary
This passage is an exposition on the obligation of believing in the guardian angels (al-ḥafaẓah) and the recorders of deeds (kutub al-aʿmāl) from among the angels. The author begins by citing a hadith that describes how Allah refined the two guardian angels so that they are seated on the person's molars, with the tongue as their pen and saliva as their ink. This metaphor emphasizes the immediacy and thoroughness of their recording. He then explains the term 'al-nājidhayn' (the two molars) through various interpretations: the last right and left molars, the shoulders, the chin, the lips, or the mustache. The hadith of Mu'adh is noted to be particularly emphatic about the tongue's role in sin. Next, the author describes the positions of the two angels: the angel of good deeds on the right is an overseer over the angel of evil deeds on the left. Their positions change based on the person's posture–walking, sitting, or lying down–as narrated from Mujahid. Another opinion states that the angels change at the times of ʿaṣr and fajr prayers, and they date the records by days, weeks, years, and places. The author then explains the phrase 'they will not neglect' (lan yuhmilū): they leave nothing of the person's actions unrecorded. The term 'act' encompasses all words, deeds, beliefs, and intentions, including the secret remembrance of the heart, which the angels perceive by a scent. Two hadiths support this: one from Hajjaj ibn Dinar about perceiving the scent of dhikr, and another from Ibn ʿUmar about the angel moving away due to the stench of a lie. Thus, the passage affirms the comprehensive recording of all human acts by the angels.

Key Terms
الحفظة
كتبة الأعمال
الملكان الحافظان
الناجذين
السمعيات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the angels only record major deeds from a distance.
Correction: This passage shows they are seated on the molars, recording even the smallest words instantly.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, where are the two guardian angels seated?
A) On the person's shoulders
B) On the molars
C) On the forehead
D) On the hands

Key Takeaway
The two guardian angels are seated on a person's molars and use the tongue as a pen and saliva as ink to record every word.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you knew that every word you speak is being written down by angels seated on your molars, what change would you make to your conversations today?
?
Your tongue has been made a pen — what are you writing with it right now that you would be ashamed to read back on the Day of Judgment?
?
The angels are closer to you than your own jaw. How does that awareness affect the next word you plan to say?

The Positions of the Angels of Good and Evil Deeds and Their Alternation
Author details the positions of the two recording angels and their alternation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific positions of the angels recording good and evil deeds based on a person's posture, and the opinion that angels alternate at prayer times.

Core Idea
The angels adjust their positions as you move, never leaving you unattended.

After describing the seating of the two guardian angels on the molars, the author turns to the distinct roles and positions of the angel recording good deeds (on the right) and the one recording evil deeds (on the left). These positions change depending on whether the person is walking, sitting, or lying down.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on angel positions
Read the Arabic passage starting with 'Wa malaku al-ḥasanāt...' and note the different positions.
2
Identify the roles of the right and left angels
The right angel is for good deeds and is an overseer over the left angel for evil deeds. Notice the authority structure.
The right angel is described as 'amīn' or 'amīr'.
3
Study the position changes
The positions change based on the person's state: walking, sitting, lying down. Also note the opinion about alternation at prayer times.
Mujahid says they do not change as long as the person lives.

?

?

?
If the angels alternate at Fajr and Asr, what does that imply about the significance of those prayer times in your life? Are you conscious of the changeover of angels when you pray? How can you make these times moments of repentance and renewed intention?

The Comprehensive Recording of All Deeds, Intentions, and Private Thoughts
Author explains that angels record all deeds including intentions and provides hadith evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the recording angels write down not only words and actions but also beliefs and inner intentions, as evidenced by hadiths about smelling the scent of dhikr and the stench of lies.

Core Idea
Nothing escapes the angels' record — not even a silent thought or intention.

The author concludes the section on recording angels by emphasizing that they neglect nothing. Writing is not limited to spoken words; it includes actions, beliefs, and even silent remembrances of the heart. Two hadiths illustrate how the angels perceive these inner states through scent.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on comprehensive recording
Read the Arabic passage starting with '(Lan yuhmilū)...' and the hadiths about the scent of dhikr and the stench of lies.
2
Understand that 'act' includes all
The author clarifies that 'act' (fiʿl) includes words and other things, so writing is not limited to speech. Consider how belief and intention are recorded.
3
Reflect on the hadiths
The hadiths show that angels perceive the scent of good and evil. How does this affect your understanding of accountability?
The angel moves away a mile from a liar due to the stench.

How do the angels record the silent remembrance of Allah in the heart?

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You now know that every intention, belief, and silent thought is recorded and sensed by angels. Think of a belief you hold that you have never spoken aloud—perhaps a doubt or a judgment against someone else. How does knowing that it already exists as a recorded deed in your book change the urgency to address it? Before you close this lesson, name one step you will take tonight to purify that inner state.
?
The angels perceive a scent from your deeds—fragrant from good, foul from evil. Consider your last 24 hours: what scent have you been leaving in your home, your workplace, your heart? Identify one specific bad habit that produces a foul scent—lying, backbiting, or hidden resentment—and commit to a concrete action to replace it with something fragrant before tomorrow morning.
?
You cannot hide from the recording angels. Is there a wrong intention you have been nursing in your heart, thinking it would remain secret forever? How does this lesson force you to stop fooling yourself? Write down that intention here, and then write what you will replace it with—starting now.

The Recording Angels: Their Function and the Obligation of Belief
Definition of recording angels and obligation of belief

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the function of the recording angels (al-ḥafażah wa al-kirām al-kātibīn) and why belief in them is obligatory.

Core Idea
Every word, action, and intention is recorded by angels who never neglect.

In this lesson, we explore the reality of the recording angels from the section on Sam‘iyyāt. The author describes their placement, alternation, and the comprehensive nature of their recording, including even inward thoughts. We will also examine the wisdom behind this recording and the obligation of belief, supported by hadith and Qur’anic verses.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the flow of ideas.
Notice the author begins with the physical placement of the angels.
2
Understand the angels' positioning and alternation
The passage explains that two angels are assigned to each person—one on the right, one on the left—and they alternate daily at certain prayers. Also, during sleep, they reposition.
This shows the constant surveillance of angels.
3
Grasp the comprehensiveness of recording
The angels record not only speech but also actions, beliefs, and even intentions. The hadith about the scent of dhikr and the stench of a lie illustrate this.
Nothing escapes their recording.
4
Learn the obligation and benefits of belief
Belief in the recording angels is obligatory. The wisdom includes instilling shyness in the believer and providing testimony on Judgment Day.
The purpose is not for Allah’s need but for the servant’s benefit.
5
Reflect on the distinction between good and evil deeds
Good deeds of believers and evil deeds of disbelievers are recorded distinctly, with forgiveness or rejection at the end of the record.
This highlights divine justice.

قسم السمعيات
أحدهما على يمينه والآخر على يساره ، وإنْ رَقَدَ كان أحدهما عند رأسه والآخر عند رجليه كما رُوي عن مجاهد (۱): «لا يتغيَّران ما دامَ حيًّا»، وقيل: بل لكل يوم وليلة مَلَكان يتعاقبان عند صلاة العصر وصلاة الصبح، ويؤرخون ما يكتبون من أعمال العباد بالأيَّام والجُمَع والأعوام والأماكن. (لَنْ يُهْمِلُوا)، أي: لا يَتْرُكونَ مِنْ أَمْرِهِ شَيْئًا فَعَلْ) المرادُ مِن الفعل ما يعمُّ القولَ وغيره، كما ذكره أولاً ؛ إذ الكتابة ليست مُختصَّةً بالأقوال، بل تكون في الأفعال ، والاعتقادات، والنيَّات، كذكر القلب سرًّا بعلامة يعرفونه بها، ففي حديث حجاج بن دينار (۲) : قلت لأبي مِعْشَر : الرَّجل يذكر الله في نفسه ، كيف تكتبه الملائكة ؟ قال : يجدون الرّيح » ، وفي حديث ابن عمر قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : إذا كذب العبد كذبة تباعد عنه الملك ميلًا مِن نَتن ما جاء به (۳).

وجوب الإيمان بالحفظة وكتبة الأعمال من الملائكة
وظواهر الآثارِ أنَّ الحسنات تُكتَبُ مُتميّزة عن السيئات؛ فقيل: إِنَّ سيِّئات المؤمن أول كتابه ، وآخره : هذه ذنوبُكَ قد سَتَرتُها وغفرتُها. وحسنات الكافر أول كتابه ، وآخره : هذه حسناتك قد رددتها عليك وما قبلتها.
(وَلَوْ ذَهِلْ حَالَ صُدورِ ذَلكَ الفِعل عنه ؛ لأنَّه ليس الغرضُ مِن الكتب الإثابة ولا المعاقبة ؛ ففي حديث ابن عباس في قوله تعالى: ﴿ما يَلْفِظُ مِن قَوْلٍ إِلَّا لَدَيْهِ رَقِيبٌ عَتِيدٌ [ق: ۱۸] ، قال : يُكتب كل ما يتكلّم به مِن خير أو شرّ ؛ حتَّى أنَّه ليُكتب قوله : أكلت شربت ، ذهبت، جئت، رأيت، حتّى إذا كان يوم الخميس عُرِضَ قوله وعمله ؛ فَأَقِرَّ منه ما كان منه ما كان مِن خيرٍ أو شر ، وأُلْغِيَ سَائِرُه (۱).
ثُمَّ هذه الكتابة مما يجب الإيمان (۲) به ، ليست لحاجة دعت إلى ذلك ، وإِنَّما يَعلَمُ حكمتها سبحانه ، على أنّ فائدتها أنّ العبد إذا علمَ بها .. استحيا ، وترك المعصية ، وقيل : لأنَّهم شهود بين الله تعالى وبين خلقه، ولذا يقالُ للعبد (۳) يومَ القيامة : كفى بنفسك اليوم عليك حسيبا ، وبالكرام الكاتبين شهودا .

Section on the Sam‘iyyat (audible matters). One of them is on his right and the other on his left, and if he sleeps, one is at his head and the other at his feet, as narrated from Mujāhid (1): 'They do not change as long as he is alive.' And it is said: Rather, for every day and night there are two angels who alternate at the afternoon prayer and the morning prayer, and they date what they write of the deeds of the servants by days, weeks, years, and places. '[They] will not neglect' (i.e., they do not leave anything of his affair; they do [an action]) – the intended meaning of 'action' is that which includes speech and other things, as he mentioned first; for writing is not specific to words, but rather occurs in actions, beliefs, and intentions, like the heart's remembrance secretly by a sign they know. Thus in the hadith of Ḥajjāj ibn Dīnār (2): I said to Abū Mi‘shar: 'The man who remembers Allah in himself, how do the angels write it?' He said: 'They perceive the scent.' And in the hadith of Ibn ‘Umar, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'When the servant lies a lie, the angel moves away from him a mile due to the stench of what he has produced' (3).
(1) He is the Tābi‘ī, the imam, the exegete Abū al-Ḥajjāj Mujāhid ibn Jabr al-Makkī, client of Banī Makhzūm, born in the year 21 AH. Al-Dhahabī said: The shaykh of reciters and exegetes; he took tafsīr from Ibn ‘Abbās and recited it to him three times, stopping at every verse asking him about its revelation and context. He traveled extensively and settled in Kūfa. He would not hear of a wonder without going to see it: he went to the well of Barhūt in Ḥaḍramawt, and went to Babel searching for Hārūt and Mārūt. As for his book of tafsīr, the exegetes are wary of it. Al-A‘mash was asked about that and said: They thought he asked the People of the Book, meaning Christians and Jews. It is said that he died while prostrating, and he died in the year 103 AH, with some disagreement; some say 102; Ibn al-Madīnī said 104 AH. (2) He is Ḥajjāj ibn Dīnār al-Wāsiṭī, client of Ashja‘ al-Buṭaykhī, among the narrators of hadith; a group declared him trustworthy, and he died before 150 AH. (3) Al-Suyūṭī transmitted it with this wording in al-Jāmi‘ al-Ṣaghīr (130/1 no. 840); and it was transmitted with similar wordings by al-Baghawī in Maṣābīḥ al-Sunna (326/3 no. 3772) and al-Tirmidhī in his Sunan (348/4 no. 19172) who said: Yaḥyā said, 'So ‘Abd al-Raḥīm ibn Hārūn affirmed it?' He said: 'Yes.' This is a hadith=

The obligation of belief in the guardians (al-ḥafażah) and recorders of deeds from among the angels. And the apparent meanings of the traditions are that good deeds are written distinctly from evil deeds. So it is said: The evil deeds of the believer are the first of his book, and its end: 'These are your sins, I have concealed them and forgiven them.' And the good deeds of the disbeliever are the first of his book, and its end: 'These are your good deeds, I have returned them to you and not accepted them.' (And even if he forgets at the moment of the occurrence of that action from him, because the purpose of the writing is not reward nor punishment. Thus in the hadith of Ibn ‘Abbās regarding His statement, the Most High: 'Not a word does he utter but there is with him a watcher ready [Qāf 50:18]', he said: Everything he speaks of good or evil is written, even to the point that his saying 'I ate, I drank, I went, I came, I saw' is written, until when Thursday comes, his speech and action are presented; then what was of good or evil is confirmed, and the rest is nullified (1). Then this writing is something which belief in (2) is obligatory; it is not due to a need that necessitated that, and He only knows its wisdom, Glory be to Him, and its benefit is that when the servant knows of it, he feels shy and abandons disobedience. And it is said: Because they are witnesses between Allah, the Most High, and His creation. Hence it is said to the servant (3) on the Day of Resurrection: 'Sufficient for you today is your own self as a reckoner, and the noble writers as witnesses.'
||
A good, strange hadith – we only know it from this chain, transmitted solely by ‘Abd al-Raḥīm ibn Hārūn. And Abū Nu‘aym [reports it] in Ḥilyat al-Awliyā’ (197/8).

(1) See: al-Durr al-Manthūr, vol. 7, p. 593. And al-Ḥāfiẓ al-‘Asqalānī said after transmitting this narration: I have not seen this connected as a statement of Ibn ‘Abbās from a reliable chain. See: Fatḥ al-Bārī, vol. 13, p. 523. (2) Yūsuf ibn ‘Umar said: Whoever denies this ruling, or doubts it, is a disbeliever because it is established by the Book. Allah, the Most High, said: 'And indeed, over you are guardians, noble writers' [al-Infiṭār 82:10-11] and by His saying: 'Angels alternate among you by night and by day' and by consensus. End. al-Afqahsī said after agreeing with Ibn ‘Umar above: 'As for the one who is ignorant of it, he is a disbeliever according to the jurists.' And the uṣūliyyūn said: He is not a disbeliever. I say: The correct view is not to declare him a disbeliever, and Allah knows best. See: ‘Umdat al-Murīd, vol. 3, pp. 1255-1256. (3) In the printed edition: 'It is said to the person'; and in some manuscript copies: 'It is said to some'.
Source pages p. 475

Commentary
This passage is a continuous exposition on the subject of the recording angels (al-ḥafażah / al-kirām al-kātibīn) under the section of al-Sam‘iyyāt. The author begins by describing the positioning of the two angels assigned to every person: one on the right, one on the left; during sleep, one at the head and one at the feet, citing a narration from Mujāhid that they remain with the person as long as he is alive. An alternative view is that they are replaced daily at the times of ‘Aṣr and Fajr prayers. The angels date the records by days, weeks, years, and places. The phrase 'they will not neglect' is explained to mean that they omit nothing of the servant's affair; the verb 'act' here includes speech, action, belief, and even inward intentions, such as the heart's remembrance of Allah which the angels detect by a scent. Two hadiths support this: the first from Ḥajjāj ibn Dīnār quoting Abū Mi‘shar, and the second from Ibn ‘Umar reporting that the angel moves away a mile due to the stench of a lie. Then the author moves to the obligation of belief in these guardian recorders. Traditions indicate that good deeds and evil deeds are written distinctly. For the believer, his evil deeds are recorded first and then forgiven; for the disbeliever, his good deeds are recorded first and then rejected. The purpose of recording is not reward or punishment per se, as indicated by a hadith from Ibn ‘Abbās: every word is written, even mundane statements, and then on Thursday the speech and action are presented and only good or evil is retained, the rest cancelled. Belief in this recording is obligatory; its wisdom is known only to Allah, but its benefit is that the servant, knowing he is being watched, becomes shy and abandons sin. Another benefit is that the angels serve as witnesses on the Day of Judgment, as stated in the Qur’anic verse: 'Sufficient for you today is your own self as a reckoner, and the noble writers as witnesses.' The passage concludes with a comment on the hadith chain, noting its uniqueness. The footnotes provide biographical information on Mujāhid, Ḥajjāj ibn Dīnār, and the grading of the hadith, as well as a discussion on the ruling regarding one who denies or is ignorant of this obligation: some scholars declare such a person a disbeliever, while others (the uṣūliyyūn) do not; the author inclines toward the latter view.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the recording of deeds is primarily for Allah to remember or to use for reward/punishment.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the purpose is not for reward or punishment (لأنه ليس الغرض من الكتب الإثابة ولا المعاقبة), but to make the servant shy and to have witnesses.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is one of the benefits of the recording angels for the believer?
A) To increase the believer's wealth
B) To make the believer feel shy and abandon sin
C) To punish the believer immediately
D) To record only bad deeds

Key Takeaway
Belief in the recording angels is obligatory; their comprehensive recording of all deeds, words, and intentions serves to instill God-consciousness and provide testimony on Judgment Day.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you are alone and about to commit a sin in secret, do you truly believe that the angel on your left is recording it? If yes, then how can you still proceed? What would it take for you to stop?
?
The lesson says the angels date records down to weeks and places. Your past year's deeds are fully documented. If you were to be held accountable for just one week of that record right now, would you feel confident? Why or why not?
?
The angels can detect your inward dhikr by a scent. When was the last time you were conscious that even your silent thoughts are witnessed? How does that awareness change your inner dialogue?

Obligation of Belief in Recording Angels
Obligation of belief and distinction of good and evil deeds

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that belief in the recording angels is obligatory and that good and evil deeds are recorded distinctly, as indicated by transmitted traditions.

Core Idea
Every deed is recorded distinctly, and the record of a believer begins with sins that are forgiven.

This lesson begins by affirming the obligation of belief in the guardian angels who record deeds. The author then cites traditions showing that good deeds are written separately from evil ones, and he reports a specific saying about how the records of believers and disbelievers are presented.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text and its translation carefully. Notice the opening statement of obligation.
2
Identify the distinction
Look for how good deeds and evil deeds are written separately. What is said about the believer's book and the disbeliever's book?
The believer's sins are at the beginning and then forgiven; the disbeliever's good deeds are at the beginning and then rejected.
3
Reflect on the purpose
Ask yourself why this distinction matters. The author is emphasizing that the recording is just and detailed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجوب الإيمان بالحفظة وكتبة الأعمال من الملائكة

وظواهر الآثارِ أنَّ الحسنات تُكتَبُ مُتميّزة عن السيئات؛ فقيل: إِنَّ سيِّئات المؤمن أول كتابه ، وآخره : هذه ذنوبُكَ قد سَتَرتُها وغفرتُها. وحسنات الكافر أول كتابه ، وآخره : هذه حسناتك قد رددتها عليك وما قبلتها.

ولو ذهل حال صدور ذلك الفعل عنه؛ لأنَّه ليس الغرض من الكتب الإثابة ولا المعاقبة؛ ففي حديث ابن عباس في قوله تعالى: ﴿ما يَلْفِظُ مِن قَوْلٍ إِلَّا لَدَيْهِ رَقِيبٌ عَتِيدٌ﴾ [ق: ۱۸]، قال: يُكتب كل ما يتكلّم به من خير أو شرّ؛ حتَّى أنَّه ليُكتب قوله: أكلت شربت، ذهبت، جئت، رأيت، حتَّى إذا كان يوم الخميس عُرِضَ قوله وعمله؛ فَأَقِرَّ منه ما كان من خير أو شر، وأُلْغِيَ سَائِرُه.

ثمَّ هذه الكتابة مما يجب الإيمان به، ليست لحاجة دعت إلى ذلك، وإنَّما يَعلم حكمتها سبحانه، على أنَّ فائدتها أنَّ العبد إذا علم بها استحيا، وترك المعصية، وقيل: لأنَّهم شهود بين الله تعالى وبين خلقه، ولذا يقال للعبد يوم القيامة: كفى بنفسك اليوم عليك حسيبا، وبالكرام الكاتبين شهودا.
The obligation of belief in the guardians (al-hafazah) and the scribes of deeds from among the angels. And the apparent meanings of the traditions indicate that good deeds are written distinguished from evil deeds. For it is said: Indeed, the evil deeds of the believer are at the beginning of his book, and at its end: 'These are your sins which I have concealed and forgiven.' And the good deeds of the disbeliever are at the beginning of his book, and at its end: 'These are your good deeds which I have returned to you and not accepted.' And if he forgets at the moment of performing that action, it is because the purpose of writing is neither reward nor punishment. For in the hadith of Ibn Abbas concerning the saying of Allah Most High: 'Not a word does he utter but there is with him an observer ready' (Qaf: 18), he said: 'Everything that one speaks of good or evil is written, even to the point that his words are written: I ate, I drank, I went, I came, I saw. Then when Thursday comes, his speech and his action are presented, and what was of good or evil is confirmed from it, and the rest is discarded.' Then this writing is one of the things belief in which is obligatory. It is not due to any need that calls for it; rather, He, glorified, knows its wisdom. Among its benefits is that when the servant knows of it, he feels shy and abandons disobedience. And it is said: because they are witnesses between Allah Most High and His creation. Hence it is said to the servant on the Day of Resurrection: 'Sufficient is your own soul this day as a reckoner against you, and the noble scribes as witnesses.'
Source pages p. 476

Commentary
This passage defines the obligation of belief in the recording angels (al-hafazah al-katabah) and explains the nature of their recording of deeds. The author states that the outward indications of the transmitted traditions show that good deeds are written distinctly from evil deeds. He then reports a statement that the believer's evil deeds are placed at the beginning of his book, and at the end it is said that they have been concealed and forgiven, while the disbeliever's good deeds are at the beginning and then returned and not accepted. The author then explains that even if one forgets at the moment of performing an action, the writing still occurs because the purpose is not reward or punishment. He cites the hadith of Ibn Abbas regarding the verse 'Not a word does he utter but there is with him an observer ready' (Qaf: 18), where Ibn Abbas said that every word of good or evil is written, including mundane statements, and then on Thursday the speech and action are presented and only the good or evil is confirmed while the rest is canceled. The author then emphasizes that belief in this writing is obligatory, not because God has any need, but its wisdom includes that the servant, upon knowing that his deeds are recorded, will feel shy and avoid sin. Another benefit mentioned is that the angels serve as witnesses between Allah and His creation, so on the Day of Resurrection it will be said to the servant: 'Sufficient is your own soul as a reckoner against you, and the noble scribes as witnesses.'

Key Terms
الحفظة (al-hafazah)
الكتبة (al-katabah)
الملائكة (angels)
الإيمان (faith)
الآثار (traditions)
السيئات (evil deeds)
الحسنات (good deeds)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that good and evil deeds are recorded in the same list or that the order doesn't matter.
Correction: The passage clarifies that good deeds are written distinctly from evil deeds, and the record of a believer begins with sins that are forgiven, while the disbeliever's record begins with good deeds that are not accepted.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens to the believer's sins at the end of his book?
A) They are written and left as is
B) They are concealed and forgiven
C) They are returned to him
D) They are discarded

Key Takeaway
Belief in the recording angels is obligatory, and deeds are written distinctly with a just order for believers and disbelievers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on your own book of deeds, do you live with the confidence that your sins—though many—will be forgiven if you are a believer? Or do you treat them lightly, assuming they will be covered without genuine repentance?
?
The disbeliever's good deeds are returned and not accepted because of lack of faith. What does this teach you about the priority of faith over outward actions? In your daily life, are you more concerned with the appearance of your deeds or with the state of your heart before Allah?
?
If the recording angels are writing every deed distinctly at this very moment, what sin or good deed have you committed today that you would be ashamed or proud to see at the beginning of your book? How does this awareness change what you will do in the next hour?
